Oh, sons, now I have completed this book for you, which is the last of medical science, because its completion has led to its end, and through its explanations, and through its declarations, it appears to me that you should understand what belongs to you in this treatise, which is part of surgery performed by my own hand.
Since the operation performed by my own hand is scattered in our region and in our time, almost entirely private, so that little light falls on this science, and its investigation remains hidden; and there remain only some brief descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which change most things and lead to those errors and misunderstandings, until their intentions are closed and the force and art of it are lengthened.
And it appears to me that you should revitalize this order of the treatise through a second way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that I may add the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools of the work as an addition to the declaration, and as preparation for it, which is necessary.
But the reason why there is not found a good craftsman in this our time to perform this work with his own hand is that the art of medicine is long and requires one's actor to be exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy which Galen knew, so as to know the joints of the members and their forms, and their conjunction and separation; and have knowledge of the bones, nerves, and ligaments, and their number and arrangement; and of the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their efflux.
And therefore says Hippocrates that a name is not a man, but rather in small things, and even more so in the art of one's hand.
But we have already spoken of that in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said about anatomy will not be spared from falling into error, through which many men will die, as I have seen many of them, because some are formed in this science and depart from that sense and experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who had inserted an abscess of scrophulous apostema into the neck of a woman, and had cut through some arteries of the neck so that great blood flowed, causing the woman to die among her own people.
And I saw another doctor who decided to remove an arrow from a man who had been wounded in his state, and the arrow was large, and it came out with a piece of intestine, so that that man died on the third day.
And you yourself had called me to remove it, and I saw that due to the largeness of the arrow and the condition of the patient, it was clear to me that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and endeavored to set the fracture of a blacksmith's leg in his thigh; and prepared the doctor with his ignorance, removed the fracture above the wound with forceps and astels with strong stretching, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then loosened the binding according to his own desires, and then relaxed the limb, and then released it after some days and commanded that we should loosen the ligament; and thus it was that the thigh and leg became apostematized, and ended in ruin.
And you were called to him, and I prepared to loosen the ligament, and succeeded in bringing about quietness and alleviating his pains.
But meanwhile the corruption was already confirmed in the member, so that I could not restrain it, and it did not cease to spread its corruption in the member until the patient perished.
And I saw another doctor who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated about three days later, so that the wickedness of it magnified its evil with its master.
Which is because the cancerous abscess is pure of melancholic humors, and therefore it does not need to be treated with any iron instrument, but rather with a member that suffers as if entirely possessed by it.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation performed by my own hand be divided into two parts: one is in operation which is associated with health, and the other is in work where danger lurks in major dispositions.
And I have already existed here in every place of this book where the operation is in error and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to keep this and lay aside that, so that foolish people may not find their way to speak and to deceive you.
And therefore take up your arms with solicitude and protection of God, and your patients with felicity and firmness.
And use the best way with God's gracious salvation and glorious succession, and lay aside terrible diseases of difficult healing, and stand firm with your arms against what makes you tremble, so that the situation remains in your faith and in your name does not deceive you: for it is more remaining to your glory, and also in this world and in the end to your sanctity.
Galen had said something about certain monodies: "Do not heal a bad disease, lest evil doctors be named".
And you have divided this book into three chapters.
The division of the book begins, and first of the first part. The first chapter ordered from head to foot, in the forms of instruments and iron tools of cauterization, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on dryness and perforation, and on cupping, wounds, and extraction of arrows, and similar matters to these, all organized and classified according to the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on cure of twisting and similar matters to these; chapter organized from head to foot, and according to the forms of instruments.
You should know the quality of the joints that require cauterization and the defects of those who are to be cauterized, and in what condition it is prohibited to cauterize.
Therefore I say that the sermon on the quality of the joints that require cauterization and the defects of those who are to be cauterized is a long and prolix discourse, subtle by science, and secret hidden; and already many wise men have spoken about it, and they have disagreed among themselves, and I will only relate a small part of their sermons, fearing prolivity.
And therefore I say that cauterization is beneficial to all complexions universally which are of material or their materials, except for two complexions which are caudal without material.
In the caudal and dry complexion with material, it is desiccated; for some say that cauterization is beneficial to it, while others say the opposite, that cauterization is not suitable in a disease that is due to quality and dryness, since the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient for a caudal and dry disease with water that is hot and dry to be healed.
And those who say the opposite, that by cauterization is made joint in all caudal and dry diseases that are found in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of man and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say by this sermon that experience has already taught me several times to discover.
But I don't think it's necessary to go further on this matter, since it has already been dealt with and exercised in the chapter on cauterization by last exercise, and understood the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of diseases in their respective cases, and the causes of these, and the accidents that occur to them, and the space of time for those.
But in other complexions, there is no fear for you, and especially in cold and humid diseases, for all doctors have agreed on those, and are not discordant about jointing with cauterization in those.
And know, sons, that the secret of cure by cauterization with fire and its goodness is over cauterization with medicine combined, for fire is simple, whose action only reaches the member that is being cauterized and does not harm another member adjusted to it, except with a small inconvenience.
But the action of medicine combined reaches to those members that are distant from it, and easily brings disease of difficult healing to the sick member, and easily endangers.
But fire, due to its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, only does what is superfluous. And it is already known to us through experiment and the long duration of service in studying the art on the truth of causes; and therefore I am excused from the length of this sermon. And if it were not that it is not read in a better book in this pause to you, a secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies and its expulsion by which diseases are expelled, with philosophical sermons demonstrated, which would be sharp in your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time when it is convenient to do cauterization and pause at the best time of spring.
And I say that cauterization is convenient at all times, because the harm caused by time accidents is submerged in the joint of what attracts to cauterization, and most especially if the cauterization is for pains or necessary pains, strong and fistulous, which do not suffer tardiness because it is feared of those who come with malice, which is greater than small harm entering through time.
And thus it does not enter into your minds, or sons, that this is not estimated except by the common people and foolish doctors, so it is that at that disease which is cured by cauterization there is no reduction at all times, and pause at its consequence.
And the cause is not thus as they say it is, for cauterization is nothing but a place of medicine that alters the complexion and dries out the humors which are the cause why pains come.
But however, cauterization is superfluous over medicine by the will of its utility and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its disease will return at some hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of his disease, and the virtue of him, and what is prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluities in him, and what has been acquired by him through food and similar causes; but if the disease that is administered cauterization is a subtle disease in a few superfluities and humors, such as tooth cauterization for pain and similar to that, it is possible that in him that pain will not return, but rather it will be done in small degree.
And the common saying is that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, and it is a desperate remedy, not in what they understand in it, because I believe that there is no cure that is beneficial through medicine or any other cause approaching cauterization.
And the cause is contrary to that; and I understand that cauterization is the last resort of medicine only when one administers the methods of cure for some diseases, and those medicines do not conduce, and approaches at the end of the cause, one cauterizes, and it profits to that. And here I conclude that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to my understanding which I understand from the common people and many foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this unless for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cauterization does not matter, as it is absolutely true, for I have already proved and demonstrated that it only matters in some bodies, and not in others; and cauterization with gold is good and better than with iron, just as they said; but however, when you do cauterization with fire on gold, it is not to your advantage, because it is made according to the quantity you want through the roughness of the gold, and because it prepares to receive cold; and if you adjust over it ignition, the gold melts by the fire, and the craftsman can see through the occupation of that.
And therefore it is fitting to do cauterization with iron in such a way that we are more lightly and more properly guided towards the rightness of the operation.
And I have already organized this chapter on cauterization according to chapters, and I have organized those from head to foot, in order that the one who demands it may find what he wants of it.
The First Chapter.
This cauterization confers on the humidity and coldness to the servile accident of which there are two causes: one is caused by a surfeit of soda and multitude of raumatic fluxes called "corissa", from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and multitude of sleepiness, and toothaches and yawning, and universally all diseases that come through coldness, just as in paralytic, sodden, apoplectic, and similar illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is this: first, I command the patient to be purged with laxative medicine, clarifying his head, for three or four nights, according to what the virtue of the patient and his age and habit require.
And then I command him to shave his head with a razor, and after that, to place himself between two stones on a flat bench, and to put his feet on the floor.
And then pause the razor's edge against the nose between your two cheeks, with your palms pressed firmly on either side. But meanwhile, as your said of the middle part is achieved, mark that place with a tent, and then apply the cauterization olive to which this is the form:
And then place it on the marked place with a tent, in such a way that it descends, by which your hand is constrained little by little, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see even a small quantity of bone being uncovered, like the amount of a grain of wheat, then immediately lift your hand, and if it does not return to that iron, with another of its kind, until what I have said to you is seen by the bone.
And then take a small amount of salt and dissolve it on the place, and let it stay for three days.
And then apply to it a poultice made of bitter border and let it stay on the place until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with quadruple medicine, until it is healed.
And they said that as long as the wound remains open, so much better is it to apply cauterization, because it is more effective and beneficial.
And some of them said that the cauterization should be done in the bone itself, and kept until some part of the specificity of the bone is softened.
And then rub it gently with that which has been adjusted to the bone, and apply the cure.
And others said that with this cauterization, one arrives at the end, until it presses strongly on the bone, until the bone cracks open, and this is the form of small alphabetic script: And they believe that from that place, the vapors of the head will evaporate.
And the wound should be kept open for a long time, and then cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two species of cauterization do not seem evident at all, except in some men according to the way of fear; and I leave it to you, I think that the better is for health, when it is; because the head is revealed by the dissolution of continuity like we have testified in other members, and especially when the head of the patient is of a fierce nature.
And the first species of cauterization is safer and better, as I think; and from that hole and with that work comes health.
Second Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Head.
When in all the head a chronic and long-lasting pain occurs, and it is prolonged in the patient, and he uses various remedies such as herbs, combs, capes, poultices, ointments, and bandages, and especially if he has already been cauterized with one cauterization which did not help him at all, then consider whether the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and it is not fierce and finds a great cold, then that cauterizes another cauterization after leaving it for a little while. And then cauterize that over the horn of his head with a cauterizer, until the bone is parted. Cut the bone and expose the quantity which we have recounted, and cauterize that with a cauterizer in the back part of the head, in the location called "vas", where the windpipe is situated. And lift your hand in this way, and do not expose the bone, because the patient by this will find a great deal of pain different from all other headaches.
And I say that this cauterization should be done in its place, because it is necessary to cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput with a more subtle cauterizer than the one used for the middle part of the head; and this is the form of it.
Fourth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Migraines that are not Ancient.
When the pain is soft in the part of the head or spread to the eye, one should purge the head with clarifying medicines and administer another cure which I have said in the divisions of diseases; and if it does not help, then cauterization is done in two ways: either with a medicine that combines acute properties or with iron.
But the cauterization with combining medicine is that you take a lump of alum, and dissolve it and remove the extremities from both ends. And then cut out the location of the pain in the temple with a well-sharpened lancet, until a small hole is made, and it is hidden under the bone.
And then apply pressure on it with a stopper that is adjusted for gradual constriction, and leave it for the space of three hours; and then remove the plug and treat the alum, and let the wound rest for two or three days, and then apply a poultice to it submerged in border until the location makes a break.
And then cure that with quadruple medicine, until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some combining medicines which I have written in the two treatises on combining medicines.
But the cauterization with iron, according to this method: ignite for cauterization of which this is the form:
and it is called "claus" or "clavish", because the head of it is like the shape of a key in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small prominence.
And then pause over the location of the pain, and hold your hand - so that it is not burnt by the heat which remains - and move the iron slowly little by little with velocity.
And if the quantity of what is burnt by the specificity of the bone is like the majority of it, and lift your hand for that reason, so that the artery which remains is not burnt, lest a flow of blood come.
And then apply a poultice to the location with salt water and pause it for three days; and then apply another poultice, this time with border, and then cure with quadruple medicine until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize at the extremity of the cutlery according to the cauterization, and be careful not to cut into an artery in this non-ancient migraine properly.
Fourth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Ancient Migraine.
When you treat migraine with what we have said about the previous cure and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not help, and the disease is so severe that it does not follow the pattern of the first cauterization with medicine or the one with fire, then it is necessary to ignite the cutlery until it is white-hot, since you are signaling on the location of the pain with a line of length which is the majority of the same, or what has been said; and pause your hand for a moment and apply pressure gently until you incise the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jawbone, which is affected by mastication, and that the ligament is not burnt and the nerves that are connected with it are not damaged, lest a spasm occur.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is cut, because in the cutting of it there is fear, and especially to him who ignores what he is doing and has not studied or tried; and leave the operation in his hands at the beginning.
And I will find a memory of the regulation of accidental bleeding from the artery according to my own method, in its own place in this book.
And if you see that this disease does not respond to this cauterization and you see the patient's body tolerable, then cauterize that in the middle part of the head just as we have recounted, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cauterization which we have said in the chapter on stretching of artery with cauterizer having two handles, and it is better cauterization this one and more suitable.
Fifth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Earaches.
When in the ear there is pain due to cold and it is treated with lactating causes and with another cure which I have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then ignite the cauterizer, and this one has no name, of which this is the form:
And then apply the point to the ignition, and be led around the entire ear like a wheel is turned, or in the circuit of each example if the pain is in one. Draw out the cauterizer along the root of the ear little by little, as you mark the place with a tent.
And if the cauterizer touches all the points in the entire ear, and wherever it is applied, then cure the locations until they are healed.
Sixth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Turtura.
Turtura which is cured and with cauterization is nothing but the species that comes through flux, according to what we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species that occurs due to dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you treat that species of turtura with jarrings and capipurgi and guarguarismes, and your cure does not bring relief, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one on the root of the ear, the second a little below the temple, and the third at the conjunction of two lips.
And pause your cauterization on the contrary side of the affected part, because softening comes only on the side that appears to be healing.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cauterizer on the right side of the extremity of the ear, a little above the horn of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger's width, and pause your hand with the cauterizer until the quantity of the majority of the bone's specificity is burned.
And this is the form of the cauterizer, and it is a species of cutlery, the form of which is presented before us. But more subtle still is that it should be used as you see fit; and it is necessary to temper it in the place of superfluous grossness a little.
And then cure the location with what is before us, until it is healed.
Seventh Chapter.
On Cauterization of Ancient Apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it with what we have said and your medication does not bring relief, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize that with four cauterizations: on all the horns of his head; and with a cauterizer in the middle part of the head, just as we have said; and with one in the crown. And the manner of the cauterization is done according to what has been said above.
And it is cauterized on the mouth of the stomach, and it is more recent; and then be cured with what proceeds.
Eighth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Oblivion caused by Flux.
Be sure to give the patient large jars and pills that serve as clarifying medicines in the beginning.
And then cut off all the hair from the patient's head and pause on the crown of it an ointment described in the treatise on ointments.
And pause that for a few days, because that is the manner of cauterization. And do it according to that method which I have already said.
And thus if they are healed well; and otherwise, then apply three cauterizations to the back part of his head, which are descended from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the neck. And pause between each cauterization the thickness of a finger, and then cure the wound with what has proceeded.
But if you wish to add more and the patient is tolerating well, then apply the cauterization in the middle part; and if you wish for even greater addition, then cauterize that above both horns.
And then cure that until it is healed; and be the cauterizer olive-shaped according to the form given before.
Ninth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Paralysis and Softening of the Entire Body.
Be sure to process the head in clarifying medicine with jarrings and what we have said; and then cut off the patient's hair, and then cauterize that with a cauterizer in the middle part of the head, and with one on all the horns of the head, and with one on the back part of it, and with three cauterizations on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the disease of softening of the body with many and those who are tolerating well, but the disease is strong, then cauterize that with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and subsequently with a cauterizer until the bone's matter of the location is burned away, and lift your hand. And then cure that until it is healed, and this be olive-shaped cauterizer.
Tenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Epilepsy.
It is not cauterized the epileptic, but that epilepsy which is due to flux.
And then clarify the brain of it at the beginning with jarrings and with another cure which we have said in the division when the disease is great and is tolerating the exception of medicines.
And if it is an infant who cannot tolerate medicines, then administer guarguarismes and mastiguation with clarifying medicine, before this for several days, with good nutrition.
And then cut off the patient's hair, and then cauterize that with one cauterizer in the middle part of the head according to the previous manner, and another on the back of the head, and on each horn of the head, may it be cauterized. And if the disease is strong and tolerating, then cauterize that with cauterizers which I say, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And be olive-shaped according to what has preceded.
But if the patient is an infant, then pause and apply a subtle cauterization according to this manner.
Eleventh Chapter.
On Cauterization of Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted and flux is gross, then cauterize that with the cauterizers which we have said in the having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluity declining to melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give him to drink that which clarifies the brain of it according to what has preceded in the division.
And then cut off the patient's hair, and then make a twisted cord decently made from it on the circle, and then pause that in the middle part of the head.
And the patient should be seated quietly, and kept from all disturbance.
And then apply a poultice; and it is more worthy to be in a border of an old sheep's fleece. And warm that over the fire by gentle heat measured according to what is suffered when it is in that place. And then place that in the middle part of the head on the circle, and let it rest until it is cooled down.
And do this with the patient for a whole week once, and then give him another regimen of it good until he is healed; or if you wish, cauterize that making small points according to what is most in him, so that you keep your hand with a cauterizer thus ordered: this is a species of cauterization which moistens the brain with equality.
And then pause that wrapped in cloth or in gray linen.
Twelfth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Water Descending into the Ear.
When you have declared the beginning of water in the ear by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give to drink to the patient that which clarifies the head of it, and keep that from all humidity.
And then place that in a bath in hot water for several days.
And then command it to cut off its own head, and cauterize that with a cauterizer in the middle part of the head; and then cauterize that with two cauterizers on both temples if it is the beginning of water descending into both ears, or of one ear if it is the beginning of water descending into one ear.
Cut with a cauterizer all the veins and arteries which are left by the bone; and let the cauterizers be in that length on the latitude of the temples.
And take care to stop blood flow when it is being cauterized; and if you see blood flowing from the wound, stop it with some medicine that is at your disposal.
And you will find wisdom in the extraction of arteries and in the abscessing of those and caution regarding blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the nape left between two bones with two cauterizers produced afterwards.
Thirteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Old Tears.
When tears of the eyes are ancient and due to the veins and arteries which are in the manifest location of the head outside and it is verified that this is superfluous watery flux, then cauterize that with a cauterizer which we have recounted in the chapter on the beginning of water descending into the ears, and with one cauterizer in the middle part of the head and two cauterizers in the nape between two temples, and with two cauterizers in the nape between two bones. And if you need to add something, then cauterize that on the entire length of the eyebrow above the edge of the supercilium with a small cauterizer.
Fourteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Stench of the Nose.
When you medicate that with what we have said in the division and your medication does not bring relief, then prepare yourself and give to drink to the patient those remedies for three nights; and then cut off the patient's hair, and cauterize it with a cauterizer of myrrh and an olive-shaped cauterizer. And then cauterize that with a clove-shaped cauterizer and two cauterizers on both superciliums, leaving a little space between the hair.
And take care not to cut into the artery.
And of the clove-shaped cauterizer, this is the form.
Fifteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Softening of Eyelids of the Eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by disease or humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with a lunar-shaped cauterizer; and this is the form of it:
And if you wish, then cauterize that over both superciliums a little with two cauterizers in all parts, and be prolonged to the temporal areas. And let the length of each cauterizer be according to the quantity of supercilium.
And do not press too hard with your hand and the cauterizer, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid is thickened.
Sixteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Eyelid of the Eye When Hairs are Converted to the Inner Parts and Strike the Eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the inner parts in such a way that they strike the eye, then cauterize them by two manners, either with fire or with medicinal burning.
If with fire of it, command the patient to look beforehand at their own hairs in such a way as those which they clarify, until they are prolonged and equalized; and if I strike that which you must not neglect, then strengthen the eyes of it with a bandage so that there is no harm until the hairs are born.
Then when they are born and equalized, then pause the patient's head in your seat, and appropriate sign above the eyelid of the eyes of it with a tent, with a signal which is according to the figure of a leaf of mirth, and be the beginning of the sign proper to the hairs.
And then wrap it in a cloth wrapped in almond oil or in a poultice of papyrus on the eye.
And then ignite the cauterizer which this is the form of it.
And then cauterize on the figure which is signified, little by little, in many times, until the surface of the bone which is like a leaf of myrtle, all appears properly.
And the sign of health of this work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already being contracted and the hairs of it being elevated above the puncture of the eye.
And then elevate your hand and leave that for three days, and appropriate wrap it in cloth until the scar is formed. And then cure that with an ointment until it is healed.
But if some cause returns to the hairs and the eyelid is softened, then do another time the cauterization on that just as you did previously.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid left behind, then cauterize that until it is elevated to its natural place and is equalized so that the hairs do not strike the eye.
But the cauterizer with medicinal burning is that which you command the patient to look at their hairs until they are prolonged and equalized, and then make a cloth of fabric in the shape of a leaf of myrtle.
And then take with known salt and fresh cause anaunt. The end. And if not, then mix those causes well, and make this with a feast so that it is not cooled down; and then spread the mixture of water on the cloth which is made in the shape of a leaf of myrtle, and wrap that around one eye or both eyes; and wrap the eye cloth wrapped in almond oil, and the patient's head be in your seat.
And then say the said words on the medicine and press that a little and do not harm it until the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for biting is in it like fire.
And then, as the patient perceives that he feels biting, then say the medicine and do not harm it until the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for biting is in it like fire. Then, when the biting ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water; and then consider if the eyelid has already been raised as washed by fire or incision, for then it is well; and if not, then return to that same location of the medicine where you did not use the medicine and do not neglect until your operation is equalized and the eye is constricted.
And then wrap that in cloth wrapped in border until the bone of adjustment is eradicated; and then cure that with an ointment or another substance until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you to, diligently guard your operation so that in the eye no residue of medicine falls; and if the eyelid becomes softened after some days and some cause of the hairs strikes the eye, then repeat your medication on that location which is softened by the eyelid, and properly as you did at the beginning, and appropriate send it to be healed.
And this is the form of a leaf of myrtle.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified according to magnitude and smallness, and therefore according to this is made your contraction.
And may not be hidden the way of rightness to that which is studied in this art.
Seventeenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Fistula Which is in the Lachrymal Gland of the Eye.
When you cure a fistula with the water which we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not concur your cure, then make sure that you cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to pause their head in your seat, and keep their head calm between two seats in such a way that there is no harm nor agitation on their head.
And then wrap it in a cloth wrapped in almond oil or in a poultice of papyrus over the eye.
And then ignite the cauterizer which this is the form:
the one that is curved, like a form of cane or a pen nib of vulture, from the one end with which the cauterizer is made.
And if you wish, it should penetrate into the other end. And if you want, it should come out like a tent.
But nonetheless, that which is curved is better for the patient's work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus and dry that one. And if it is not open, then make an incision and extract the hardening from it.
And then place the cauterizer on it which is well ignited, and take with that one a little bit of the cauterizer to the head at the side of the nose, so that you do not err nor disturb the patient, and then place the cauterizer in the gray parts of the eye and corrupt that one.
And then, if at the beginning of your cauterizer it penetrates into the bone, that is good; and otherwise, then repeat the cauterizer one or two times if necessary; and leave that as such for three days, and then wrap that in cloth wrapped in border and surround it with an ointment to dry until it is healed.
But if it has passed 11 days and is not healed, then wrap that in sharp corrosive medicine so that the bone is uncovered and is scraped according to what is written in your own chapter.
And there is another manner of cauterization of fistula which some others say: go to the location of the fistula and fill it up and then wrap that in a subtle fissure, which is the form of it: Pour into that the quantity of one inch of melted lead; and take with your hand a piece of good retention, and do not harm the patient because the melted lead does not penetrate the eye of him; and make sure to wrap over the patient's eye a cloth wrapped in almond oil or water, for the lead adheres to the location of the fistula and cures that one by miraculous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and cure, that is good; and otherwise, then it is necessary to administer a blow of the nose and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose according to its own proper place.
Eighteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Wound of the Pox.
Many times accidental cracks occur on the lips, and especially on the lips of children.
And then, as you treat those cracks with the water which we have said in the divisions and your cure does not take hold, then ignite the small cauterizer like a cutlery according to this form that is shown:

Nineteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Fistula in the Mouth.
When in the root of uvula or on the palate or in the roots of teeth an apostema forms and breaks, and is antiquated, and the wound opens and becomes a fistula, and you cure it and your cure does not take hold, then make sure that you ignite the cauterizer according to the quantity received in the fistula, and place that ignited one in the opening of the fistula, and take with your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and at the end of it do so once or twice; and then cure that with the water which we have said for the cure, until it is healed.
And then, if the pus is abscessed and is healed, that is good; and otherwise, then it is necessary to uncover the location and expose the corrupted bone according to what is written in its own chapter.
Twentieth Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Teeth and Softening of the Gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are damaged, and you cure them with medicines and it does not concur, then make sure that the patient's head is in your seat, and then ignite the cauterizer in the shape of which will come to this, so that you place the quill on the tooth and insert into it the ignited cauterizer quickly, and take with your hand a little bit until the patient feels the heat of the fire at the root of the tooth being reached.
And then lift your hand, and then repeat the cauterizer several times according to your will.
And then the patient will fill their mouth with salt water and keep it for an hour, and then stop, because the damaged tooth is closed and the softened gum is strengthened and the corrupted moisture is dried up.
Twenty-First Chapter.
On Cauterization of Toothache Pain.
When toothache pain is due to coldness, or it is hot or warm, and your cure with medicine does not concur, then there are two ways of cauterization: either cauterize with the edge of an ox's hide, or cauterize with fire.
Cauterizing with the edge is that you take the edge of an ox's hide and boil it in a cauldron made of iron, and then take a cloth and wrap it around the tip of the tentacle, and then immerse that boiled edge in boiling water, and place that on the painful tooth quickly until it is cooled down.
And then repeat that several times until the virtue of fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, immerse the wool or cloth in the boiling water mentioned above, and place that on the painful tooth, and place over that hot iron until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But nonetheless, the cauterization with fire is that you attend to the glowing coal or iron, and it be in the heart of it some grossness and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cauterizer in the shape that comes, and place it on the tooth and take with your hand until the cauterizer is cooled down; and do this several times because the pain will be relieved either on that day or the next day.
And make sure that by the impression of that cauterizer, the patient fills their mouth with good bread and keeps it for an hour, and then spits it out; and this is the form of the cauterization.
And cauterize as you wish, with whatever means are possible to you.
And this is the form of the quill:
Twenty-Second Chapter.
On Cauterization of Extrophuli.
When extrophuli are covered with flesh and cold humors, and do not obey digestion by medicines, and you wish to aid the digestion of those slightly, then you ignite the curved cauterizer in the shape which is as follows, having two extreme parts that emit smoke from one end and take it up through the other end, and place that ignited cauterizer on that apostema once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the apostema.
And if the apostema is small, then place the cauterizer according to the quantity of the apostema, and let it be for three days and place over it a cloth wrapped in border until what has been burned by the fire is relieved.
And then cure that with an ointment, tents, and cloths until it is healed.
Twenty-Third Chapter.
On Cauterization of Hiccup and Constriction of Ale.
When the humors come up to the top of the lung, and especially when this is due to coldness of congestion, then make sure that the patient is evacuated at first with laxative medicines, and then cauterize that at the root of the esophagus in the affected location.

And then cauterize that with another cauterizer at the junction of the neck at the last vertebra. And the cauterizer for this should be sharp, in the manner previously described.
And then cure that with water as has been previously indicated until it is healed.

And then cauterize the cord until it penetrates into the other side; and the figure of cauterization will be like this: two heads, one on top of the other, with a long handle.

Twenty-Sixth Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Stomach.
When cold and many humors come up into the stomach, causing it to protrude from its natural position and become multiple rumblings there, and if you continue with the methods of cure and they do not concur, then make sure that the patient is turned over onto their back, and stretch out their arms and legs, and then cauterize that with three cauterizers: one on the feet for the quantity of a finger with a sharp cauterizer, and two on both sides of the cauterizer, so that it forms a triangular figure; and leave between them so that they do not touch each other to avoid creating pressure.
And if the depth of the cauterizer is equal to the quantity of two thirds of the thickness of the cord.

Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Fretful Liver.
When the liver becomes painful due to coldness or moisture or gross evacuation, and its normal function is interrupted by excessive egress, and the patient is cured with water as we have said and does not concur, then make sure that the patient is turned over onto their back, and sense three cauterizers according to this form and this quantity placed on the liver below the hipochondriums, where it is customary for a man to recline.
And the space between each cauterizer is according to the thickness of a finger, and the cauterizers are placed according to the length of the straight body.
And do not compress the cauterizer with force.
And if the quantity of water that is added equals the quantity of the thickness of the cord's substance, and it is not more adjusted; and if the patient remains standing on their feet; and if they are not sitting, then lie down, which has already stretched out its legs, and raised its arms.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauterizers with a cauterizer like a small knife, when you are in your subtlety and prudence in the art.
And take care not to proceed too quickly in the cauterization, and be mindful of the subtlety of all the cord's substance, so that it is applied throughout the body and reaches into the vessels, for this cord here is subtle; and know this.
Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
On Perforation of Apostema of the Liver with a Cauterizer.
When there is excitation or apostema in the liver and you wish to know if that apostema is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunica, then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the patient will experience gravity and pain with sharpness.
And if it is in the tunica of the liver, then with great sharpness and pain, and often to the point where you exhaust even the most skilled physicians.
Then make sure that the patient is turned over onto their back; and sense the location of the apostema with a tentative touch; and then ignite the cauterizer which is like a rag, in the shape which has been previously indicated on another page. And do not use this form of cauterizer unless you have studied it in the art of medicine and many maladies have known it; but this one has been daringly tried on this operation some times, yet still leave that to us, and it is sweeter.
Twenty-Ninth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Pleurisy.
They say that the ancient cauterizers of the ribs of Aristology have made plauresi cool in this manner, and it is this that you take from the ribs of Aristology, a long dry rib that is found, and it is as thick as a finger.
And then immerse that in oil and ignite that at the fire, and then cauterize with a cauterizer in that location which is between the continuation of the furcula and the neck; and with two small cauterizers, one slightly declining towards the part below the beard, and with two cauterizers in that location where it declines between the fifth rib and the celiac artery, declining slightly towards the back parts; and with another cauterizer in the middle location of the foot; and with another above the stomach, and with three cauterizers on the back parts; and with one cauterizer in that location which is between the two shoulder blades, and with two cauterizers from both sides of the foot, leaving the cauterizer which is between the two shoulder blades.
And do not compress your hand with the cauterizer, but rather be in the manifestation of the cord's work.
And it is said by certain ancients that some men of great skill have used a cauterizer made of iron like a ray and ignited it, and placed it in that location which is between the ribs, until it reaches that apostema and purifies the healthy part, just as we have said in the apostema of the liver.
But in this perforation with a cauterizer, there is no fear, for it happens so quickly that the wound is made in the location of the fistula, to which there is no healing.
Thirty-Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Mole.
When you cure the malady of the mole with water as we have said in the division and do not concur with your cure, then make three or four cauterizers according to the length of the mole, following the figure of the cauterizers of the liver, the figure of which has preceded.

And there is another manner of cauterizing, which is that you ignite the cauterizer having two vertiments, which cause we have mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle, and lift up the cord which is at the end of the mole, where the patient lies to the left.
And be your elevation the one by which you lift up the cord according to the length of the body, so that cauterizers are made according to the latitude of the body.
And then enter between the two vertiments, ignite one, into that which with those you penetrate the cord of the other side.
And then extract the cauterizer; and thus four cauterizers are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cauterizer having three vertiments.
And then cure the cauterizer more than it has laid down to take away the bruise for too many days, because it is more certain that the other causes preceding in the cure.
Thirty-Second Chapter.
On Cauterization of Hydrops.
Cauterizers do not cauterize in hydrops, but rather only in the proper location.

And the quantity of the depth of the cauterizer should be proportional to the subtlety of the cord.
And then leave the cauterizer unburned, so that it takes away the bruise for a long time.
And do not evacuate the patient's cure from the cauterizer with water as is required for two intentions, and it will be hastened to him with assistant healing.
The form of the cauterizer with which the belly is cauterized is sharp like the one that precedes it above, and it is this one with which the back is cauterized is oval-shaped, according to its previous form.
Thirty-Second Chapter.

When in nature there remain old ulcers or one of thick humors that are inflamed or corrupted with moisture, and they are cured by the methods we have said in the division and do not concur with your cure, then cauterize with three cauterizers on the pus left below the triangular vertebrae of the back and small triangular shape, and above the navel going down two fingers' width.

Thirty-Fifth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Athletes' Wounds Near the Abscission of Their Own.

Thirty-Sixth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Fistulas that are formed in the natural parts of one's body.
When nature does not obey the work that we have recommended in its place, and the patient is frightened by this, then heal with a cauterizer.
Therefore, when there is some fistula in the natural parts of one's body that is old and corroded with pus and corrupted moisture, then it is more fitting to cure it with subtle probing and to know the quantity of its depth as previously mentioned.
Then ignite the cauterizer that resembles a ray. And then insert the ignited cauterizer into this fistula, and according to the quantity in which it enters the probing.
And continue to insert the cauterizer into that fistula until those corrupted bodies are completely consumed in one, two, or three applications, according to your necessity.
And be careful not to burn the nerves and veins; or if the fistula goes into the bladder or into the intestines, then be cautious of all those places; and do not make it so unless the fistula is in a fleshy location and you think it is not penetrating.
And then cure that place until it is healed.
And if the place is sealed, and the matters from there have been abscessed away, and it remains like that for a long time, then you should know that it has been entirely cured.
And if the matters are not removed from there, then you should know that it is penetrating or in the precursor of corruption, or coming forth from those causes of which remembrance will be made in its place.

Forty-First Chapter.

And then take dried goat's wound and infuse it with fire until it is made into charcoal; and then pause him on the wool and leave it in until it is stretched. And then repeat this process, and do not cease until the sensation of the mordication reaches into the hip and relieves the pain.
And this manner of cauterization is called cauterio of goats.
Forty-Second Chapter.
On Cauterization of Two-Pain.
Sometimes pain is in both shoulders due to various causes, such as by bruising or striking or by excessive evacuation, and by causes similar to those, by infusion of wet and humid matter.
And the cauterizer is not applied except in this single species which is made for effusion of wet matter.

Fifty-First Chapter.
On Cauterization of Purification.
When some purification is delayed in maturity, and thus it is due to the superfluity making that so, or due to the state of the patient, because he is old in decrepitude, with little blood, or by time, and you want to hasten the maturation of purification; then cauterize in the circle of it with many small punctate cauterizers; and then leave it alone, until it will fasten in maturity.

Fifty-Second Chapter.
On Cauterization of Corrosion.
Corrosion is a walking corruption in the member, which eats away that place just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you find that corruption in the location which bears a cauterizer with fire, then you ignite small to moderate-sized cauterizers, and large ones according to what is convenient in that location where the corrosion is.
And then cauterize that place completely until you eradicate all the corrosion and there remains no cause of it.
And then leave that place alone for three days, and pause over the locations that have been cauterized with a soft cloth mixed with oil until all the scars are eradicated and all the corruption.
And then cure that place with remedies generating flesh.
But if after three days the flesh appears to be healthy and there is no corruption in which it grows, well and good; but if not, then reapply the cauterizer to that place where the corrupted areas remain.
And corrosion is treated with acute medicine for several times, because that is a halfway point in the location of the cauterizer. But still, cauterizing with fire is a lighter remedy.
And I have already said the cure of it with acute medicine in the division, and therefore take that when you will have need.
Fifty-Third Chapter.
On Cauterization of Warts and other Similar Afflictions.
Many times it happens that a malady called warts affects the parts behind the foot, and is a great and deep-rooted cause which besets the foot; and cauterization in those places is done in two ways, either with fire or with hot water.
But cauterization with fire is when you ignite the cauterizer in a concave shape like a small pen, which is made of iron according to the quantity that contains the wart on all parts, and has subtle margins.
And then pause the ignited cauterizer over the wart, and then move your hand with the cauterizer in a circle around the wart until the cauterizer reaches the depth of the wart. And leave that place alone for three days until you start to see it fall off. And then apply an emplaster to that place with wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the emplaster on that place for one night, so that it will be eradicated from its roots.
And then cure that place with remedies generating flesh until it is healed.
And if it does not convert, and many times it happens on the surface of the body, especially in the arms and legs, then you must administer cauterizers with water, which is when you take a cannula made of iron or bone or wood, and place that over the wart; and then put a small amount of hot water into the cannula, and grasp your hand firmly around it, so that you compress the margin of the cannula against the root of the wart, and let the hot water flow down to the root of the caustic substance; and wait for the patient to experience the burning sensation of the hot water for about an hour, and then remove it, because the wart with its roots will be eradicated.
And thus do the same for those that are in the other locations, until you have treated all of them on their own in the body.
And then cure those places where the roots of the warts are eradicated with this water of remedies which generates flesh.
Fifty-Fourth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Tremors.
When you find that someone is afflicted with tremors due to a blow on the nerves or due to fever caused by a blow, or for some other similar reason, then it is good that you cauterize him with four or five cauterizers placed between each vertebra of the back, one cauterizer per vertebra; and also cauterize in his feet, and on his stomach, with an olive cauterizer.
And the tremors of him will cease and hasten the recovery from the blow-struck illness.

Fifty-Sixth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Blood Flow Accidents due to Arrow Injuries.
Many times it happens that an arrow wound is inflicted which cuts off the limb beyond which it is, or which cuts through apostemes or cauterizers of the member, and so forth, and it is difficult to heal that.
Therefore, when such an accident occurs, then you must take with your hand the cauterizer from the arrow's point of entry, and place it on that location with great force, so that many times it is applied until the flow of blood is stopped, and there is no further bleeding.

And if the blood is expelled from the artery's orifice when you remove the said cauterizer and extinguish it, then take another cauterizer carefully from the cauterizers that are prepared in the fire, and do not cease to perform this action until the blood is restrained.
And beware that you do not burn the nerves which are here, and that you bring another evil upon the patient.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, it is not possible to restrain the bleeding in those places, and especially when the artery is large, unless with one of four methods: or with a cauterizer as we have said, or by extracting the blood, because when it is extracted, the extremities are burned and the bleeding is restrained; or that it be tied with a ligature or with a gentle constriction; or that medicines be applied to it which have the virtue of restraining the bleeding; and be strengthened with a poultice and decent binding.
But he who administers a decent binding with ligature and constriction with cloths or by position of causes combining and similar, does not heal unless slowly.
But if that should happen to someone and there is no doctor present nor medicine, then take action with the pause of the said indication on the orifice of that vein as we have said, and understand that it must be done with great constriction at the top part of the wound until the blood stops flowing from the superior part of the wound; and above the arrow wound, sprinkle with cold water of great freshness so that the blood is congealed and thickened; and then care for what has need of cauterization or medicine.

Fifth Chapter.
