Sixth Chapter.
On the Cure of that which cats in the Ears.
The whole cause that cats in the ears is one of four species, because it is either mineral pyre or a similar cause, such as iron and copper, or it is of plant origin, such as cheese or fava, or it is a fluxible cause, such as water and vinegar and their likenesses, or some animal.
And therefore when pyre cats in the ear or some other cause similar to those causes that do not agree nor believe in the ear, and pause the ear at the sun, and if sometimes the pyre appears, then you should distill into it some cause of violet oil or samian, and administer the extraction of it, and make the stornutary condensation, and stop up the nostrils beforehand for the event of stornutation. And then pause in the cavity of the ear some cloths or woolen things, and stretch the ear to the parts above, because many times it is forgotten with these causes.
And if it is not gotten, then you should administer the extraction of it with the instrument called gestes epicicaries, subtle ones whose form is this:
And if it is forgotten with gestures, be it so; and if not, then you should administer the extraction of it with a subtle needle of little duplication.
And therefore if it is not forgotten by this, then you should make a tube of iron and insert the extremity of the tube into the hole of the ear and seal around the tube with wax and softened oil, so that only the tube is open. And then extract with your tongue, by a strong attraction, for many times as we have recounted.
But if it is not forgotten in this way, then you should take some halved or prepared wick with which the birds are taken by a small quantity, and put that in the extremity of the ray, and then wrap around that decently placed piece. And then insert that into the hole of the ear with ease, and then express the ear of its moisture.
And therefore if it is not forgotten with all the causes that we have recounted, then you should cut away before it ends in putrid aposteme or spasms.
And the manner of cutting away is that you at first should let blood from the saphenous vein and extract it according to the method of the virtue of it, and then make that cease between your hands and convert the ear into the parts above, and finally make a small incision in the root of the ear, so that the grey matter of it is released at the location previously prepared. And make the incision of lunar shape into which it reaches the pyre, and when the pyre is blackened, stop that if you can with suitable instruments; and then close the incision at that hour with speed, and cure that until it is healed.
And if the cause catarrhous in the ear is one of the fat things that you believe and are inflamed, then administer the cure and extraction; but if it does not obey your sight, then you should take a fine spatula, subtle ones whose form is this: and administer to it the abscission of that fat thing which has fallen into the ear.
And do not do this when you think that it is already moistened by the vapor of the ear, and pause in many cloths, and then extract from those with needles or subtle gestures, or with incision as we have said, because the extraction of it is facilitated.
But in the water which has entered into the ear, it is necessary that the patient uses stornutation with condition at first, and fills his own ear with some old cloth, and pours over that ear the water in which there is the pyre, and if by this it is forgotten, be it so; and if not, then you should take many fine pears and lemons according to the length of the finger, and burn those in the fire for a little while, and the patient inserts one of those into the hole of his own ear and strikes on one side with another pear on the pyre which is inside the ear. Therefore, do not cease until all the water is forgotten.
Therefore, do not cease until all the water is forgotten. And already the water will be forgotten in such a way that you take of paper or gauze, i.e., and place one end of it into the ear and stretch the other end over the fire until the wax is burned away.
And then place another gauze and make it so many times until all the water is forgotten, and stretch that with a tube just as above is said of the extracting pyre.
But in the extraction of an animal that enters into that ear, if it is small, like this one and its kind, cure it just as we have said in the division; but if it is of great size, which causes appear to the sense of feeling, then you should administer the extraction with gestures and needles, and the cause of it is more gentle than all other causes that catarrhous in the ear.
But in the extraction of a worm generated in the ear, when you cure it with that which we have said in the division and in the treatise on distillations, and your care is not confirmed, then you should look at the ear to the sun.
And therefore if any cause of the worms appears here, then you should extract it with gestures or subtle needles; but if no cause appears, then you should take a tube which is stretched and above it has this form: And insert the subtle extremity into the ear according to the quantity which can be suffered by the patient; and then suck it with a strong suction, and make it so many times, until all the worms are forgotten.
But if it does not obey you by sight, then you should block and seal the circuit of the tube with wax just as we have said; then administer distillations which the ancients have already tried in the cure of worms, and you will find this in the treatise on distillations.
And be your effusion with which you pour the medicinal oils into the ear with this instrument whose form is this: And make that of silver or iron, stretched and above it has a small hole, and with a plate on top.
And therefore be like what is needed in the cavity of the tube of continuation here where it will be necessary. And if you wish, take the rod and wrap it around the extremity of the tube decently placed, and then pour oil into the cavity of the augmentation, or juice of some herb, or whatever you want from these medicines in the tube - and that is in the ear -, and then insert the rod with a decent shape above and express with your hand that with gentle pressure of it until the oil is expelled into the cavity of the augmentation and the patient feels the oil outside.
And what is put in the ear has already been calcined with fire for a little while. And take care that the cause which you will distill in the ear is not too fierce, for the medicines of the ear do not suffer this.
Seventh Chapter.
On the Cure of Earwax Obstruction.
Sometimes some children and young men are born with their ears unperforated by their mothers, and this already occurs in some men, earwax obstruction in the meat of the ear due to wound or flesh not being in that place; and this obstruction sometimes is made in the forehead of the ear which does not sense the feeling, and sometimes it is in the outer parts.
And that which occurs in the forehead of it, which does not comprehend the feeling, is in the greatest disposition of difficult healing.
And when you can feel the feeling, it is necessary that you pause the ear of the patient in the sun and look at it. And therefore if apparent obtusion appears, open that with a subtle spatula whose form is this:
If the extremity of it in which is a small latitude, one part being sharp and the other not; and the spatula has two lion's claws for that it does not trouble the ear.
And therefore if the obtusion is due to flesh born in the ear or in the meat of it, then you should take that with subtle needles and incise it with vehement facility until all the flesh is removed.
And if obtusion is in the forehead of the ear, then you should take a subtle rod like a lion and heat it with fire for a little while, and then place that in the meat of the ear.
And therefore if you have detected obtusion with what the patient feels with facility, through gravity of auscultation, force the oppression of it with facility; and take care that you do not harm the nerves of the ear.
And then pause in the ear with cloth of linen according to the quantity of the width of the hole which you have wrapped around with Egyptian ointment; and do this for some days until you are sure of the consolidation of the wound; or take some cerote and insert it into the water and powderize over it, and use it; and if the ear is already apostemated, then you should extract the cerote and replace it with another cerote which you have wrapped around with red oil, until the apostema is quieted; and then cure that until it is healed.
But if there is a flow of blood, then you should submerge a sponge or cloth in hot water and pause over the ear, and use another cure which restrains the flow of blood, which is said in the treatise on distillation.
Eighth Chapter.
On the Cure of Athazil, which afflicts the eyelids.
Athazil, which affects the eyelids of some people sometimes being moist, and at other times being dry.
Therefore, take those with tenhallas or needles, and incise them with a spatula of their own roots, and then pause over the places as described.
But if pain with a flow of blood comes, then you should cauterize those with a lunar cautery needle.
And the best cauterization is when you insert them into the incisions and many times return, as long as there remains some cause of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Ninth Chapter.
On the Cure of Grandeyssa, which affects the eyelids of people.
Many times it develops in the eyelids of people some cause which is similar to grandessa in its strength and hardness, and because of this grandessa it is called.
And it is an aggregation of great moisture on the eyelid below and above.
Therefore, the operation in them is that you should consider if the grandessa is proceeding from there on the eyelid and is produced to all parts; and the cause of it is light.
Therefore, make an incision over it with a fine knife by the latitude, and then extract that of all parts with facility until it is evacuated, and then suspend that with a needle and cut it off.
And if the figure is large, then you should adjust it with a suture; and cure that until it is healed.
And if it is small, then you will not suffer evil from it, because the substance of it restores that and incorporates.
And if the grandessa is declining towards the outer parts of the eyelid, then you should remove the surface outside, namely, you will have to make an incision in the eyelid and suspend the grandessa with a needle, unless you are inclined to make another incision, and push that away from all parts; and if the eyelid is elongated due to the incision, this will bring about no benefit in any case.
And then wash the eye with salty water; and cure the place with that which incorporates until it is healed.
Tenth Chapter.
On the Cure of Axcirnah in the Eyelid above the Eye.
Axcirnah is a greyish growth which is generated in the tunics of the eyelid above, and most often afflicts children, aggravates their eyes, and causes them to lose their sight; and they cannot gaze at the brightness of the sun because tears are shed upon them.
And therefore you should cause them to lie upon their faces all the time, and upon their faces they sleep; and thus on the eyelids of theirs below are wet overhanging lids, which have already covered inflammation, and there is a threat of obvious abscess in the eye; and when you press the place with those very words, you will cause abscess to develop within them.
And some manner of operation is in that which the patient places their head in the tie and then pauses a cloth of linen and of water to make a calque, and makes from it a circle according to the quantity which contains arthernach of all parts, and then pauses that on top of that and presses with the very words of total power so that abscess is aggregated in the middle of the circle; and then ends in the midst of that humidity with a spatula inserting into a fissure by latitude, and the fissure is not greater than the one made in flabotomy.
But in the beginning it is necessary that you make a cut in the cord completely until you arrive at abscess, because in the most difficult processes abscess proceeds by fissure according to the form of white grease.
Therefore, extract that with cloths which you have wrapped between the very words and the outer parts, and turn it around between your right and left hands until it is dispersed.
And take care that you do not adjust in the fissure for fear that with the spatula you will not reach the eye and will displace that.
But if the abscess does not appear to you at the beginning of the fissure, but rather that you adjust in the fissure a little with facility until it processes; and then extract that as we have said; and then submerge cloths of linen in water, make them white and pause them over the place and strengthen those with powders.
And thus some that trickle salt and pause it in the cavity of the fissure so that what remains of that humidity.
And then cure that until it is healed.
But if apostema cauterized occurs in the place, then cure that with gentle poultices until it is healed.
Eleventh Chapter.
On Manners of Touching the Eye.
When in the eyelids of people there are no natural hairs and they become old, then those who are not skilled in the eye and cause to develop mannerisms of illness such as excessive tears and softening of eyelids and skin until it becomes a cause of destruction of the eye which is called touching the eye, and there is cure in four manners: or by cauterization with fire; or by acute medicine according to what was said before in the chapter on cauterization; or it is made by atactini through incision and suture; or by cannas as I will say.
And therefore it is necessary that you pause the head of the patient in the tie; then convert the eyelid of the eye with your left hand, and if it is converted, good is; and if not, insert a needle into that which has faith at the furthermost part of the eyelid below the palpebra, and make the needle penetrate through the faith above, and thus be - on the edge of the eyelid where there are no hairs - on the hairs, and pull the thread to the upper parts with the eyelid, and convert that with the ray.
And then end in the outer part of the eyelid below the hairs adjusted with spatula inserted into the lacrimal major into the lacrimal minor; and then extract the thread and pause below the eyelid with small powders of cotton or cloth, and then sew over the eyelid with tent, and be as such as a figure of myrtle.
But nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity of heaviness of the eyelid, because this already varies in men, because some of them need to have incised a great quantity from the eyelid according to the quantity by which the eyelid is softened.
And then end with the spatula on the two lines that you have sewn, and start from the lacrimal major into the lacrimal minor. And if your incision is next to the natural hairs just as it is the greatest thickness of the king.
And then put the needle in one of the two angles of the cord, and then extract that whole, and then adjust with the incision the two lips with a subtle thread or yarn, and wash away the blood, and make adhere what is superfluous from the threads over two overhanging lids with some causes seeing, if you wish to do so, and otherwise, do not cure.
And then loosen the thread of the stitches within three days or four, and then cure that.
And if you wish, leave the wound open of its stitches, and cure that with what dries and constrains, because the eyelid is lifted from the sealing of the wound and the aggregation of it; but suturing is better. And therefore I say to those who are old-fashioned in touching.
But nevertheless, in him there is solicitude over the patient, and it is of good operation, and not of fear.
And there is another manner in touching, and it is that you sew on the eyelid a figure as such as myrtle leaf, and then lift the eyelid with three fingers separated and gathered according to this form:
But if it is not possible to have three fingers, and it is not matched, then take one needle with thread and put that in the middle of the figure, and insert the other thread next to the lacrimal major, and the second thread next to the lacrimal minor, and adjust between the very words the threads with equality, and then lift all the cord over which it is sewn as we have recounted.
And then adjust the two lips of the wound with stitches, and cure that until it is healed.
But if apostema occurs from your incision or your wound, calm that apostema with cerote and similar things, and with gentle poultices.
And sometimes the eyelid is converted so that its natural hairs are changed, then it is necessary to use in it what we have said of incision; but suturing is more artificial.
Atactini with cannas is according to this form: and it is that you convert the eyelid and cut out the figure which is below according to what I have recounted; and then, by art, make two cannas or two thin astals of which the length is according to the length of the eyelid and the latitude of their being smaller than the latitude of the spatula. And you have already incised in the extremities of each part, where you have the threads.
And then add each one with subtlety above what is superfluous from the eyelid of the eye, and tighten the cannas of each part with a very strict tension, and leave that for some days, because the cord by the tension will die and become denuded and will be able to fall back into its place when it has set.
But if it is delayed, then break the cord with the tornoras, and then cure the wound until it is healed.
Therefore, when it is solidified, the eyelid is lifted and the hairs do not prick.
And this is the form of two cannas which you will make according to this form: and have the quantity of length and latitude neither more nor less.
Twelfth Chapter.
On the Lifting of Prickly Hairs in the Eye with a Needle when the Hair is Hard.
When the hairs are unnatural, hard and prickly, and cause trouble to the eyes, then the operation in that is that you take a subtle needle and pause it in that thread of gentle and fine cotton, and then adjust the extremities of it and note each one in a manner very subtle. And be the length of the threads of the quantity of one palm.
And then you will compose another thread subtle below it in brief, and bind the extremities of that if you wish.
And then pause the patient's head in the tie, and be prop of the sun so that your work may be declared, for it is a subtle and small operation.
And then insert the needle into the root of the adjusted hair which has required engineering, and make it penetrate into the eyelid rapidly until you extract that above the natural hair.
And then pull out the hair up and insert it into its place, and be the hairs one or two or three, but not more.
And then pull out your hand with that until the hair is taken out and placed in its place in the eyelid along with the natural hair.
But if it is taken out of its place and not pulled out the hair, pull out the thread from the parts below with the needle that you have composed in that, until it is pulled out from above.
And then look at that with the vision of the eye, because you will pull out the thread and the needle, and make each one and close the eye, and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place and grows over that good flesh.
And if the hair is too short, then you will adjust one long hair from the natural hairs, and it will be lifted with that, or that will leave until it is lengthened to a certain space, and then you will lift that.
Thirteenth Chapter.
On the Cure of Ichor which appears in the Eyelid above.
When it appears in the eye ichor, and it is contraction of the eyelid when it is constricted above or to the right or left side, due to bad consolidation of wound or section or cauterization, and it is called leporina, and this ichor is either natural or accidental, and it is caused by consolidation of wound or sections or cauterizations, or by semblance to their maladies.
And the manner of operation in this is that you will break down that consolidation and separate the lips of it, and place a piece of linen cloth between them, and tie those together until they are healed.
And it is not necessary that you use a cure for this from the causes which dry and constrict; because if you do so, it will return worse than never had any time without.
Use in that a cause which softens as is fenugrec, and mix with water in which are cooked high and seeded with linen or yoke of aquilon, which is liquefied with some oils, and immerse the cloth in it, and cure with that.
And the treasure of your cure is that you will perforate with all engineering that is not consolidated according to the form that was at the beginning.
And this operation which we have said is nothing but some correction of ichor that does not return to its original form as it was before.
Fourteenth Chapter.
On the Cure of Ichor which is made in the Eyelid below.
This ichor which is made in the Eyelid below, which is truly called vertadierment ichor; and it is either a natural or an accidental one.
But accidental is made by wound or section or cauterization or by other semblances.
And the way of operation for this is that you take a needle with double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right tear duct, until the thread reaches both ends of the flesh.
And then extend the flesh to the parts above with the needle and sew it with the needle, and insert it with a spatula wide. And therefore if the figure of the eyelid returns as it should be, good is; and otherwise, take the thread and pause it in the cut figure, and with that convert the eyelid, and close the two incisions on the left side of the eyelid below.
And be the extremities of the two incisions at two angles of the incision which you have made until they converge, and be made an angle of theirs so that when they come together it is formed a figure of theirs.
And this figure is Greek letter: lambda.
And then stop the flesh at that point which is the edge of the eyelid below, so that it will not exceed the width of the eyelid.
And then adjust the separated parts and sew them with the wool thread; and then cure those with that which we have said of soothing medicines and poultices until it is healed.
And if ichor appears through a fissure or suture or cauterization, then it is necessary that you open with a flat fissure over the hairs of the eyelid according to what has preceded. And then separate with a poultice between two lips according to what we have said.
In the summary of the sermon on the cure of ichor when it is above or below, that flows into operation in accordance with the preparation of the form of ichor, and that is in the form of diverse movements.
And the skilled artisans prepare engineering in every possible way to make it return to its natural form or close to it, and that sick person according to what is convenient for the operation and tools in the greatest dispositions.
Fifteenth Chapter.
On the Adhesion of the Eyelid to the Conjunctiva or Cornea.
When this adhesion occurs in some people, it is necessary to solidify the eyelid above with a thin layer of albumin from the eye, and prohibit its natural movement and works, therefore it is necessary that you insert the extremity of the thread below the eyelid, and lift it up or stretch it with an instrument.
And then you will insert the adhesion with a subtle spatula, which is not too sharp, having obtained a small obtuseness so that the patient is not disturbed by the operation, and withdraw the spatula so as not to touch the eye with its sharpness.
And be your incision such that it excises that adhesion with ease, so that the eyelid returns to its natural form and all the adhesion is healed.
And then you put salted water in the eye, which you wash with; or distill it into one drop dissolved in water.
And then separate between the eyelid and the eye with a poultice of linen, and pause over the eye wool infused in albumen of egg white, and then use for three days causes that consolidate until it is healed.
Sixteenth Chapter.

Know that the nail is according to two ways, for either it is nervous, and is similar to dry subtil ciphac; or it is non-nervous, similar to white condensed humidity, which when you touch it, or it is forced to take an oath, is cut off and the oath is not fixed in place.
And both species do not begin until the lacrimal gland, and then gradually decrease as it covers the vision and prohibits light and movement of the eye.
But the manner of operating in this incision is that the patient puts their head in its place, and then you will open the eyes of it, and lift the eyelid with your hand, and then collect the nail with an oath of little duplication and extend it to the upper parts. And then take a needle and insert into it a piece of horsehair or ox hair or cow hair, or similar, or strong thread, or duplicate the extremity of the needle little by little and put it in the middle of the nail, and penetrate it with the needle, and tie the nail to the thread; and extend it to the upper parts, and excise at the edge of the nail which sees the pupil. And then you will follow that with the hair until the very end of it.
And then you will incise the remaining part in the root of the lacrimal gland with a subtle spatula or small forceps, and free the natural flesh of the lacrimal gland so that through the incision of it no continuous flow of tears ensues.
And after some days the nail with the single oath or thread, as we have said, and then it will be excised with a lion's spatula, of which this is its form:
And beware that with the spatula you do not touch the corneal tunic and cause a rupture in it, and that the pupil is perforated.
And then the incision will create in the eye a little bit of salted water or made from sinew, and let it rest until the next day; and then cure that with what is needed until it is healed.
And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle into it, nor is it fixed with an oath, then many times this type of nail is cured with medicines, and thus it is healed as we have said and recounted in the division.
And if you want to incise it, then you will operate on the eye of the patient and take a subtle lion's spatula with sharpness according to this form: With subtlety. And if sometimes it is rarefied and is congealed and enters into its root, then you will distill from your hour in the eye of sinew or with raw silk or with salted water, and drop the eye into another day.
And then iterate on that the operation until all that is of it is removed, except that the contrary apostema remains in the eye, for then you will let it be, and cure at first the apostema until it is healed.
And then repeat your operation on that with reason until it is healed.
The eminence of the lacrimal flesh, if it is noticed in the eye by great harm, shall be suspended with an oath; and incise that part, and do not finish the incision for fear of flows of tears.
And then distill in the lacrimal raw silk and sinew, until it is healed.
Seventeenth Chapter.

But the operation in this is that the patient puts their head in its place; and then you will open the eyes of it and collect all that flesh with convenient oaths to that, and take that with a forceps or basket; and then incise the flesh at first until everything is finished with the scissors, and beware of the eye so as not to touch it with your operation.

But however you must ensure that all curing of the eye is done by natural or accidental means, working with iron, and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that member to be sufficient for that operation.

But if it is not possible for you to collect all at that hour, then you will apply all the remedy that soothes the pain of it, and leave it for some days until the pain of it is assuaged and there is no fear of apostema.

Nineteenth Chapter.
On the Reduction of Rhinitis to the Nose.
When you cure arisati with cauterization or acute medicine as described in the previous narration and it does not heal, then there is no engendering in it except that you will open on the apostema of it at its maturity, and extract all the humidity which is in it and pour into it until the bone is uncovered.
