The Exit of Twins or Multiple Fetuses. Know that sometimes twins are born, and occasionally three or four, but this is rare and not to be expected; however, there are causes that are natural, and not alive.
And consider those cases where twins are multiple, one second part, and they are separated by ciphac, distinguish them from the umbilical cord of each of them. And sometimes they are forgotten in this way as if it were a single fetus for slow natural extraction, and sometimes they are extracted in an unnatural manner as we have recounted.
And if they are difficult to deliver, or any of their parts, then you must proceed with the childbearing and arrive at what we have said about unnatural shapes, then cure those as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does that which makes it easy and subtle, and with slowness, and is skilled according to all shape as prepared by nature leading to health.
A Reminder of What is Formed in the Womb from Embryos and Abortions.
Some women are formed to give birth in one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and up to ten children, and I have verified that one woman aborted at the sixth month and another gave birth to all ten, which was caused by measuring the glorious wise men.
And all this must be in the science of the midwife, for then it will be a small resemblance to that, and therefore pause there with what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the Extraction of the Fetus when it is Dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medicine and it is not otherwise extracted, and you are forced to use an operation with your hand, then it is necessary for you to consider whether the woman has a healthy virtue and is not afflicted by any of the accidents for which on her there is feared perdition.
Then it is necessary for the woman to be evessed on the light on her back, and her head inclined downwards, and her thighs elevated.
And the minister should hold that with two parts, or bind it to the light, in order that the body of her may not extend too far from the extraction of the fetus.
And then moisten the mouth of the mare with warm oil and poultice of althea and fenugreek and sesame seeds.
And then have the midwife insert her hand with those oils and poultices into the mare, and gently insert her hand with ease into the mare, and carefully seek out the exact place where the fingers should be placed on the fetus.
And finds the convenient place there: then you consider if the fetus is prepared to descend on its head, and then place your fingers on the temples, or on the back, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or under the chin, or on the furcula of it, or on the places proper to the ribs, or on the hypochondria.
But if the descent is over the feet of it, then place your fingers in the pendentia or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary to hold the fingers with the right hand, and pause the curvature of it in that place which is between the digits of the left hand, and gently insert the hand with ease into one of those places which we have said, until you arrive at the cause of the boyd.
And then pause and place another finger or the third one if necessary, in order that there may be equal attraction, and not extension according to its straightness as much only.
And then it is good at all parts, in order that the extraction of it may be facilitated as it is done in dentures for the eradication of it.
And it is necessary in that which is between them to soften the extension; and if some part of it is retained, then the midwife should moisten her fingers with oil and gently insert those parts expertly and rotate around that which is retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fetus is forgotten, then the fingers should be pushed into that place where it is higher up; and do so until all the fetus is forgotten.
But if the hand is exhausted in front of the other, and it is not possible to reduce that part by the contraction of it, then it is necessary to wrap a cloth around that part; and then extract that until all is forgotten, and insert it either into the joint of the hand or into the armpit.
And do so in the other hand and in both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is contraction in the extraction, or it is in the head of it that the water is adjusted, then it is necessary to insert between the fingers a spatula with spines and cut the head and extract the water, or use an instrument called "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of other instruments in the chapter that is appropriate for this.
And similarly do so if the fetus has a large head by nature: then it is necessary to insert that into an almug or take that with an alundat as we have said; and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is extracted and constricted at the furcula, then it is necessary to cut into it until the moisture which is in the feet is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obeying to extraction, then you should insert the head as soon as possible according to what seems best to you.
And if the afterbirth is apostematic or is in water-dropic form, then it is necessary to perforate that until the moisture which is in it runs out.
But if the fetus is on its feet, then the attraction of it is slight and the direction of it to the mouth of the mare is slight.
But if it is constricted at the belly and feet, then it is necessary to extract that with cloth which you have wrapped around your hand, and cut into the belly and feet until the water that is in them runs out.
But if the other members are still and return to the head, then place it with your left hand; but if the mouth of the mare is opened wide, then insert your hand into the belly of the hare, and seek out that head, and draw it with your fingers into the mouth of the mare, and then gently insert one or two fingers and pull it with them.
And if the mouth of the mare is constricted by apostematic swelling which occurs to it, then do not trouble yourself over it; instead, consider administering an effusion of moist and fatty causes. And administer poultices; and follow the patient in waters that soften and humidify.
And if the fetus is on its side, then it should be possible to extract it; and administer the water which we have said for the living fetus.
And if this is not possible, then insert into the pelvis and extract.
And it is necessary not to leave any cause behind the second part.
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer the water which we have said for the cure of apostematic swellings which occur in the mare.
And if a flow of blood occurs, then stop it by administering stiptic waters and provide the other cure.
And I myself have seen a woman with a dead fetus in her womb, and on that very spot another embryo was newly formed, and on the spot where death is, there is another fetus. An abscess occurred in the left side of the umbilicus; it swelled up and became infected until it began to discharge pus.
And I was called upon to cure him, and I treated him for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
And then I wrapped him in some poultices of strong attraction, and extracted from him one bone, and after a few days, I extracted another bone; and I was greatly amazed, for there were no bones in the womb.
And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
And then I stopped the wound, and extracted many bones from him, the woman was lying in her bed with all her might, and already she lived in such a manner for a long time, and only a small amount of pus remained.
And I did not marvel at this being strange, but rather because in this is science and assistance to what the physician uses his hand for healing.
On the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
The shape of the ventouse by which the mare is opened:
This is the shape of a strengthener in which the strings are equalized, and to this equalization there are two ventouses at the ends of two feet. However, this ventouse should be more subtle and made of stricter material, such as ebony or boxwood.
And it should be the width of each wood equal to two fingers and the edge of each one a finger, and the length of each is one palm and a half; and in the middle place of two woods are two adjustments of those woods which are already fixed, the length of which is slightly less than a palm and a little more, and the width of each is equal to three fingers or a little more.
And these two adjustments should be inserted into the mouth of the mare so that it can be opened to receive those when you revolve the two prescribed ventouses.
Another shape similar to that one, but more subtle and lighter:
It should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of forceps. However, at the end of it there are two adjustments like those, and the length of these adjustments is one palm, and the width of each is three fingers.
And when you want to open the mare with those, then gently lift the woman onto the light, letting her feet hang loose, opening that which is between the thighs. And then, with your hand and the instrument, as you would do with forceps, adjust it according to the quantity you want of the appreciation of the mouth of the mare, until she does what you want.

On the extraction of the second part.
When the second part is retained during delivery, then it is necessary to command the woman to retain her breath and prop herself up with pillows, and strengthen your hand on her mouth and nose, and if this does not come out, so be it.
And if not, then take a vessel and perforate it in the covering with a hole and pause in that herb, burning the mouth of the mare, like calamus and rue and anise and chamomile and Arabic aloeswood and cassia. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the vessel, and pause that over the fire.
And then place a reed cane into the mouth of the mare, and keep it until the vapor comes to the concavity of the mare.
And then make her snort as we have said, and the second part is extruded with speed.
But if this cure does not work and the second part remains retained, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a poultice of althea, and gently insert that into the womb and search for the second part, and when you have found it, take it and extract it little by little. But if it is annexed to the womb of the mare, then gently insert your hand according to what we have recounted, and when you have found the second part, extract it gradually, so that the mare does not collapse from the vehement attraction. Moreover, it is necessary to be prepared on both sides, right and left, with ease.
And if the mouth of the mare is constricted, we have already recounted the cure with snorting and medication from the vessel with herbs.
But if it is not extruded with all the causes which we have recounted, then beware that you do not fatigue yourself over that in iteration of abstraction, but rather it is necessary that what has issued from there to the mouth of the mare lies at the thigh of the woman, and then crumble it with a mixture of equal parts and tetra-pharmacopoeia; for that will cause it to putrefy after some days and be dissolved and extruded.
But when it has putrefied, it is elevated to bad odor at the head and stomach, and that leads to the disease of the patient; and then it is necessary that sub-fumigations and suitable remedies are administered for that.
But some of the Ancients have already discovered sub-fumigation with nitre and dried figs.
Form of instrument by which the woman is sub-fumigated for the retention of menstruations and the second part:
It should be made of birch or iron.
And it should be placed with the thin end in the womb and the broad end over the fire, and the sub-fumigation should be placed on the arms of the fire.
And keep that until the sub-fumigation is consumed and another one is repeated.
On the cure of the child's anus not perforated.
Many children are born without their anal openings perforated, which are already covered with a thin and opaque membrane. Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce with her finger that membrane; and if not, pierce it with a sharp spatula, and take care not to touch the lacerta.
And then place on that a poultice of wool saturated with vinegar and oil; and then cure it with a mixture of equal parts until it is sealed.
But if you fear that it may become obstructed, then place a reed cane into the wound for many days, and remove it when the child wants to defecate.
And if there occurs an obstruction of the anus due to consolidation of wound or abscess; then it is necessary that this consolidation be inserted, and then cure it with water as we have said in the cure and with lead.
On the cure of the fistulas which are left over.
The fistulas that remain after the separation, being lower in location and thicker than those which are located near the anus outside or in the space of one part.
And it is a fistula or multiple fistulas.
And since this swelling is aged and drained of white or slightly yellowish watery discharge, and sometimes some of these fistulas are penetrating.
And those that are penetrating are known by what comes out of them through excretion and flatulence; and sometimes the patient experiences excretion, and very little is emitted from those red ones.
And some of those fistulas sometimes penetrate into the space between the bladder and the urethra, and into the opening of the vulva; and some of those that are penetrating go through the junction of the thigh and into the notch of the groin.
And in order to distinguish between a penetrating and non-penetrating fistula, you should insert your finger into the anus, and gently probe with a thin instrument of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no turbidity.
But if there is turbidity in that, then gently insert a lead or horsehair thread into the fistula until you feel the thread or hair on your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all or there is no process of excretion or emission of blood or wind, as we have said, then you should know that it is non-penetrating, and then apply the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the opening of the vulva, then the significance of it is emission of urine from that and prohibition of it to that place where the medicine has been consolidated.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the thigh or into the bone and causing pain in the circuit, then the sign of it is that the thread will pass through here if there is no turbidity in the bone, and causing pain in the circuit of the part; and that from there pus will always be present; and that it will not hold with this medicine, nor be consolidated with a poultice.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the cure for those is hard work and tediousness of the learned physicians on which we have fixed.
But in those that are not penetrating and not aged, healing with iron is hoped for according to what you have recounted to me, and the things which I have already tried.
And it is that the patient lies between your legs on his back and raises his knees up to yours, with his thighs inclined towards his belly, and then you insert a lead or iron thread into the fistula if there is turbidity in it, until you know the place where the thread passes.
And if the patient feels the pain around his navel, then it is necessary that you insert your finger into the navel.
And if you feel with your finger the thread already having passed through and penetrating, or something else between your finger and that siphac or flesh, then you will know certainly that it is penetrating; and then do not trouble yourself with that, for there is no healing in that, as we have said.
But however, some have said that it is healed in some men, though.
And the medicine by which healing is expected in that is that you apply a thin cauterized instrument according to the size of the fistula, as we have previously said, and insert it into the fistula until it comes around the navel; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those adjusted flesh adjustments are already fitted together like the feathers of an owl.
And then cure that with cloths wrapped in butter until all those adjusted flesh adjustments are fully healed; and then cure it with medicines generating and consolidating the skin, and if it is healed, good is; and otherwise, it is not healed in any time by another treatment.
And if the thread goes in and does not penetrate into that which is in the anus, but between it and the thread which is a thin layer of flesh or membrane, and sometimes the fistula opens on the surface of the codena, then dry up the codena from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it drying up with the thread, and be inside the fistula until the drying reaches the location where the extremity of the thread is, and through the thread is liberated and freed.
And then clean up those flesh adjustments which are assembled like the feathers of an owl and do not remain from any cause.
But if there is bleeding sometimes that comes between you and your operation when you are processing those flesh adjustments, then take the milh that is and use the lightest instrument to cauterize with fire or acute medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts two good habits: it is adjustment of those adjusted flesh adjustments, and abscission of bleeding by excessive moisture.
And then cure that with cloths wrapped in butter or three-layered fabric until the location gets dry, and then cure the wound with a poultice of hard skin that generates and consolidates.
And such medicines are those in which there is astringency and excess; when that has been restored, it is already healed and you do not fear relapse.
But if the fistula has already penetrated into the anus and is elongated from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and inspect with it.
And therefore if you find the thread and it is between you and her, being a thin layer of membrane or flesh, and is suitable for penetration, then there should be no operation in that place except by way of faith and hope.
The cause is to administer in that place one of three ways: either to cauterize it as we have said; or to dry it up until you achieve the conquest of the area so that it becomes possible for you to insert the thread and the healing procedure; and do not proceed with drying if there is no consent from the patient's will, and that which occurs above the navel's contents; and then cure it with what we have said, because it will be soon healed; or elongate that membrane and clean up that pus as you dry it up to the anus, just as we have said, either with a thread or another instrument of sharp extremity; and then thoroughly clean those flesh adjustments which are in the drying area until you can see through the crust; and then make an effort to restore the entire wound by drying, and if the opening above does not become consolidated, and the fistula remains open on the side of the anus, and it will be easier for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is closed in this way: when you insert the thread into the fistula, it is on the edge of the anus around the surface of the body with the codena and on the margin of the anus, then take hold of the perforated extremity, which is like a needle preparing the arteries according to this form:
and then insert it into that faithful wrapping of flesh or around those; and then insert the thread with faith in the fistula until you achieve the conquest of that place.
But if it is penetrating in the margin of the anus towards the back, then you withdraw the thread from that track just as you insert your finger into the anus; and withdraw the extremity of the thread and adjust the two extremities together, strengthening each one, and leave it like that for a day or two, and when you have inserted the thread into the flesh, strengthen it until those flesh adjustments are inserted between the two extremities of the thread and collapse.
And then cure the wound so that it is consolidated and healed.
But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in whatever way you are prepared, but not in the anus, because it is not for you to do that; and then make it so that it is healed.
The form of the spatula with which the fistula is opened: its curvature is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that you do not insert what is not necessary, just as sometimes.
On the suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows during the insertion of those.
Hemorrhoids are according to two ways, because either they are between the anus resembling charcoal, or else those are like grass growing in the rectum. And those are small and large, and the blood flows from them always and is one, and many, and outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
But however, those that are outside the anus are according to the months of little humidity, from which a yellowish liquid or a small amount of blood with continuous flow, and according to the color of the body.
And the cure for that which is behind the anus is that you command the patient to settle down and to expose himself so that his anus opens up and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take hold of them and suspend with your fingers or what you have of the nails of your finger, and then cut those which are to be cut.
But if the nails are not to be taken hold of in those due to their moisture and softening of those, then take those with rough cloth or with a coarse comb or with woolen flax, and extract those with your fingers, and then cut those which are to be cut; and afterwards powder some powders on them, suitable for the insertion, so that they are adapted to those in place of cauterization; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterizing. And then cure those with the other cure so that they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey the urge to go out, then anoint the patient with a little scratching cream and wash it with that water which is in the anus, so that it will gradually obey the urge to go out when the patient presses.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of their being is light, and it is that you take them with your finger or take them with nails and insert them, and then cure those with water as we have said, so that they may be healed.
And whoever will perform the insertion, must administer suturing of them according to this manner: take a faithful thread and insert it into an needle and then extract the hemorrhoids at the upper parts, and make that penetrate with the needle in the root of the other part, and wrap around the two extremities of the thread on the more distant part, and so latitudinally; and strengthen the hemorrhoid with a strong stricture, and then remove the needle and thread.
And do this to all of them, and leave one and not tie it, so that the superfluity of blood may flow from that.
And then pause over the anus with cloth infused in rose oil or cerote; and pause that over the anus and command the patient to rest. And then leave it until it is closed; and when it is closed, cure those with a poultice or with another cure so that they may be healed.
And when they are old and not good in that medicine, then you must reason those with the point of spatula or with your finger so that they are made moist and be hosted by those above the erosion which prevents consolidation; and then cure those until they are consolidated.
Then you must hold those with reason more violent than the first one until much blood flows and they are exfoliated; and then cure those until they are healed.
Know that alamermar is key, and it is not so except for noting the redness around the color of the skin resembling a cap of claveil, and it is made throughout the entire body and especially in the areas where there is more fat and less flesh, and one must proceed by those pains to understand the nature.
And then it is necessary to excise what is in the circuit of the key, and it must be held with forceps or nails, and it must be eradicated from its root; and then cure that.
And if you wish, cauterize according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterizing.
But of warts, it is a small, hard, fistulous, rounded excrescence on the surface of the body, and many times they appear in children.
And the cure for it is to stretch and insert that, or to strengthen that with a thread or with peel until it closes. And if you wish, cauterize it, according to what we have said, with fire or acute medicine.
But of a tumor is a small, fatty or fistulous prominence on the surface of the body growing towards the anus, and when the flesh finds that it is bitten in the manner of a formiga, and it is made around the body.
And the cure for it is that you take a tube of goose quill or of vulture's feather, and make it strong, and pause that over the tumor until it contains the circle of the tube in the parts of the body; and then turn your hand with the tube so that you insert what is in the circuit of the tumor, and pause that in the anus of the flesh, and that eradicates the tumor from its root.
And if you wish, do it with an iron or copper tube according to this form:

And if you wish, cauterize the tumor according to what is said before in the chapter on cauterizing.
On the form of the instruments that are administered to give scratching.
Sometimes it is made scratching of silver or lead or melted iron or beaten; and sometimes it is made with small and large instruments according to those that are administered, for what is administered in the cure of small children is small; and of those whose buttocks are rough or painful, the scratchings of those are small.
The form of scratching great and little:
The head of the tube above, in which the bag is tied, should be wide according to this manner; and there should be a distinction at the point where the bag is tied just as sometimes.
And the extremity of it below, which is inserted into the anus, should be dull (not open) like a lion's mouth, going back to subtlety; and on one side of it there are two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays and thicker than thin.
And the bag in which the medicines of beast's urine or sheep's wool are placed, and the root of it should be one palm.

And then the patient should be lifted up onto his back, and raise his legs high and pause there for a moment; and then one should anoint the extremity of the cauterization with oil or albumen of hen or with mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances; and then insert that into the anus with ease, and then the minister should take the bag and express all that is in the scratching instrument into the bedpan; and then extract the scratching instrument and the patient should lift his legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces it to pass, hold on until he can no longer; and if he sleeps with that all night, it is more favorable in judgment.
But if you scratch that in the illnesses of purging of the belly and the evacuation of it, then you must repeat the cauterization until it is healed.
And if in the anus there are hemorrhoids or apostemes that are hardening, then make the scratching very subtle and lion-like, like the scratchings with which children are comforted.
On the cure of the plaques.
And I have already said in the division of the cure of plaques what is suitable for the free person, and I say thus: the cure of those with me and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore, I say that plaques are diversified according to how they are made and according to the place on which they appear.
And the causes for which many times plaques are made are thus: as a result of excessive heat, or inscision with a space or knife, or percussion with a hammer, or with a stick, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many other causes.
But the plaques that are on the parts of the body are like this: a plaque that appears on the head, or neck, or arms, or belly, or legs, and similar to those of the members.
And I am recommending the cure for some plaques, because you pause that rational and rule on other plaques.
And I am starting with the plaques of the head, simple ones, because the memory of the complex ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore I say that when a simple plaque appears on the head and is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to excessive heat or similar cause, and already the swelling has increased so much that it becomes a great plague and you fear for the patient's life, then take care and bleed the cephalic vein at once, and do not delay; and extract from that blood according to the quantity of the virtue of it, unless some other cause prohibits bleeding, especially if the blood that is issued from the plaque is little.
And make the bleeding on the opposite side of the part that was plagued; and take care to prevent the patient from taking in food or drink too soon.
But if some other cause prohibits it, then reduce the food and do not approach meat or wine.
And pause over the plaque if an apostema cauterizes, and apply a poultice with rose oil alone or with wine in which it is stipticated.
But if it is certain that an apostema cauterizes, then pause over the plaque, if it is recent and the air has not changed that powder which I recommended previously in a small quantity.
And if the air has already changed that powder, then pause over another poultice until it is healed.
But if the plaque is great or is due to inscision of space and similar causes, and the lips of it are not adjusted by pus, then adjust those with a suture according to what I recommend for their suturing.
But if the plaque has already been discovered from bone and skin, and there is only a small suspensory ligament, then insert that and then cure the plaque with medicines and restore the flesh in its natural place, and command the patient to eat foods that are gross: caps and forms that resemble their own, until it is composed.
And if you find in the code decomposition and it does not adhere to the bone, then you must insert all that is putrid and remove it, and then cure that.
But if in these plaques there is an artery or vein from which blood can flow and it has not been severed by medicines, then you must inquire about the artery, and if you find that it is not severed, then insert it with spatula, or tie it; and if necessary, cause what we have said not to be done, then you must cauterize until the blood is severed.
And if these plaques are simple and small, then the cause of them is light; therefore, powderize over those this powder, for it will consolidate before the air changes those.
And the method of the powder is this: take one part of dragon's blood, two parts of saint's blood, and three parts of unextinguished fire; grind all together with a mortar and pestle until it becomes fine and powdery. Then fill the plaque with that powder, and compress it with good constriction until it adheres well to that place, and coagulates with the blood.
And then strengthen that above with powder and loosen it, and do not remove it while it is in this state, because the medicine has not yet been absorbed by the flesh until it is healed.
And sometimes make this powder alone, when you do not have in front of you dragon's blood and saint's blood.
And then perform this same operation on large plaques when it is necessary to pause over them and compress them, and these are recent plaques with their own blood, which the air has not yet altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially in summer time, then it is not advisable to place this powder on them, but rather cure those with what we have said, by applying some gentle poultices or by applying powders made from oat flour mixed with water and honey until they produce pus; and then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
But if there is a fracture in the bone, and it is small, then you must extract that with gentle force.
And I will say the cure for fractures of the head in what is to come.
On the plaques of the neck.
But if the plaque occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in medication, and between the plaque of the head when it is simple.
But if the nerves of the neck are cut or an artery is injured, then if it is a nerve, do not proceed with surgery but rather avoid curing it with what makes violent stiptication, like vinegar and egg white that is like vitriol and similar to it which does not harm the nerves and contracts it. And do not pause over the plaque any cause of total freezing, because the substance of the nerves is cold and its continuation is to the brain, which is the most noble part of all the members.

On the cure of wounds and the quality of purging with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged so that it forms a collection of pus, and then it breaks open and perforates, and the pus flows out, and the wound remains as if it were a vessel, with a thin layer of skin over it like a subtle cloth, and does not lead to further corruption, nor does it impress on the bone or nerve or ligament, it is called an abscess, and is not named fistula.
But if the space is prolonged and the corruption presses on some member, then it is called a fistula and not abscess.
And the cure for it is that you excise the entire skin layer as it is rolled back, and especially when it is thinned out and made like cloth, and make sure that it does not adhere to the location due to its corruption.

And then you take from him the water that is necessary and dissolve it with equal parts of water and honey; and poultice the abscess with that, and strengthen the opening of it, and leave the medicine in it for the quantity of two hours.
And then extract the poultice from it; and make it like that for so many days until the abscess is purified and the stench is removed.

And if the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the water of ash, then poultice it with water and honey, mixed in equal parts, and apply that; or poultice it with vinegar and honey, mixed together, because of the property of honey that purifies and cleanses, and the vinegar makes the abscess adhere, and especially when there is excess moisture and dryness in the vinegar.

And about ventilation and the qualities of using those.
Ventilation is from horns, or from earth, or from vinegar.
And ventilation is done in two ways: one of them is by scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is without scarification.
And this ventilation that is without scarification is done in two ways, because either it is with fire or without fire.
And the ventozas that are administered with scarification and extraction of blood are 14 locations in the body, of which one location where pauses are made is alnocrati, and it is the last part of the head; and the middle location of two parts of the neck together; and ventozas of the mento below the mandible and below the mouth; and ventozas of two spatulas; and ventozas of alohoster, and it is above the end of the coccyx; and ventozas of two foils, and they are from two brasses; and ventozas of two cavities; and ventozas of two cuoyssas.
And ventilation does not extract blood, but rather from small, scattered veins in the flesh, and therefore it is not able to capture virtue through these, just as it is captured by phlebotomy; nor is it necessary that ventilation be done with fire or without fire in any disease caused by repletion, until the body is completely evacuated.
But if necessity requires ventilation for disease or continuously, I administer that in every hour at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle location of it, and at some time.

The species of fractures are many, and their figures are diverse, and their causes are distinct, for some fractures are caused by percussion of space, and the percussion crushes all the bone within the skull, which is left without a bony covering, as if it were in the fist, and therefore this type is named ascial; or the space incises some part of the bone, and incises the flesh of it and does not pass through to the other side; and this species of fracture is named levatio absoluta.

And harm will come to the skull, as it is corrupted by the bone and especially when the cure of it is neglected, and there is a blackness on its surface; and therefore consider now if harm comes to the patient from the accidents we have said, know that it is pernicious for all doubt.
And if there is no blackness but from the medicine that is paused above, and it is in virtue of that medicine that makes that blackness, then you should take a part of honey and a part of rose oil, three times. And with those lines, draw a cloth (am aquels linieys un drap), and then place it on the skull (e aprop pausa aquel sobre le ciphac); and then cure it with the species of medicine that is necessary until it is healed.
Capitulum Tertium
Of the Restoration of the Nose when it is Broken.
Know that the nose is not broken except when two parts are together and superior, or one of those in some places, because there are two bones, so that the part left is cartilaginous, and it is not broken and does not cause harm to it, but only roughness and tortuosity and sinuation.
But if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you introduce the little piece into its own nose, and that you equalize that fracture outward with the said indication, and with the said powder outside, until the nose returns to its natural figure. And make it so for yourself with facility, and beware that you do not harm the patient through your operation.
And if the fracture is in the uppermost part of the nose (e si la fractura es en la pus sobirana partida del nas), and it does not go to that, then it is necessary that it be equalized with the extremity of the ray (le dit no perve ad aquela) at the place where there is a little thickness.
And if the fracture is in two parts, then make it seem as though you are doing so.
And count yourself lucky if you can restore it on the first day of the fracture, if possible; and if not, then wait for the 7th or 10th day before giving rest to the apostema.
And then insert a piece of cloth into the extremity of the nose, if the fracture is in one part, or two pieces, if the fracture is in two parts, and it should be in the thick part of such quantity that fills the track of the nose.
And I say to some of the ancient restorers that the pieces should be wrapped in wool and should be moistened all day, but it is not seen by me; having need that the piece be wrapped in albumen of egg mixed with flour and powder of mill; and then leave the piece until the bone is set and the cartilage is strengthened.
And sometimes put it into the nose, instead of a piece of cloth, a penalty more than that which is wrapped in linen cloth; and so that already you have a fracture of the nose more violent and the patient is not prohibited from inspiration.
And this cause is not necessary for you; and if you wish, do so, and if you wish, do not.
And if another apostema is formed cautiously, apply the nose with cerote or cotton dipped in vinegar and rose oil, or with dayquil.
But if there is no apostema cautious, then it is necessary to apply that outside with farina of sienna and powder of ash cypress mixed with albumen of egg; and then place it on top a lion's stopa, and do not let the nose be stopped by any cause.
But if the bones of the nose are broken with a small fracture or comminuted, then it is necessary to cut on those, and extract them with instruments that are suitable for those; and then close the wound, and cure it with what embodies and consolidates, and apply a plaster accordingly.
And if there is a blow behind the nose, then it is necessary to cure that with cloths and administer lead canules until it is completely healed.
Capitulum Quartum
Of the Restoration of the Jawbone when it is Broken.
When the jawbone is broken and the fracture is not accompanied by a wound, look closely to see if the fracture is only on the outside and has not split in two and curved inwardly, then its understanding is slight.
And so, if the fracture is in the right side, then you should insert the left indicator into the mouth of the patient; and similarly, if the fracture is in the left mandible, then put the right indicator into the mouth of the patient; and press gently with that on the curvature of the fracture inwardly along the outside with your other hand, and decently equalize it.
And if the fracture of the jawbone is already separated into two, then it is necessary to administer extension to both parts according to rightness until it is possible to equalize them.
And if there is concussion of teeth to disruption, then strengthen those that remain with wire or thread; and apply cerote to the broken jawbone, and apply a double layer of cloth over it, and place a great star-shaped pad or a single sheet of sole equal in length to the mandible; and apply it above according to how you are accustomed to binding it and according to what is necessary for application, until it is not destroyed.
And command the patient to use rest and quietness, and pause food until the lion's appetite is satisfied.
And if you think that the figure is already altered in some manner, then you should cut it off and remove it on the third day; and apply what has been altered to that, using powder of mill, albumen of egg, or farina of sienna, as long as you have the cerote of that, and pause over the application a lion's fleece.
And then, having adjusted and fitted the plaster on top of it, and the disposition of the bone is not altered, leave it alone, without disturbing it until it is healed and the fracture is strengthened; for many times this fracture takes three months to heal.
And if another cautious apostema occurs, then administer what we have said many times in the sedation of it until it is healed, and be restored to its original state.
And if the fracture is accompanied by a wound, then consider whether it is a separated piece of bone or a splinter, then you should carefully remove those splinters with what is necessary for that in the removal of them from the instruments.
And if the opening of the wound is narrow, then you should enlarge it with a flea-bottle according to the quantity of your necessity.
And then, when you have removed those splinters and they are no longer present, you should close the opening of the wound if it is large; and if not, pause over that one of the plasters that are necessary for that and embody that, until it is healed.
Capitulum V
Of the Restoration of the Furcula when it is Broken.
Many times the furcula is broken on the side in front of the muscles, and that fracture is made in one of three ways.
Where the break is single, or separate, or separated into two parts, but there are no splinters; and it is easier to restore it; or it is like that where there are splinters, and it is difficult to restore it; or it is like that where the fracture is accompanied by a wound.
And the operation in that case, when there is no wound, is to have two ministers present, one of whom should hold the assistant and tie the broken collarbone, and the other extend the neck towards that side.
And then, equalize the fracture with those very words until the form of it is made according to what is necessary, and there is neither prominence nor concavity in it.
And if you need more extension, then it is necessary to pause the titillating of the patient with a cloth or wool, and be the size of it according to the quantity of your necessity; and extend and elevate the collarbone and compress the sphere with your hand until you equalize the fracture according to what is necessary.
And if you cannot pull the extremity of the collarbone to the outside parts, because it is impeded by the breastbone (preon), then it is necessary that the patient be raised up on their own shoulders, and pause over the muscle of it a counter-pressure in great size.
And the minister should apply the muscle of it to the parts behind until the bone of the collarbone is elevated so that it is in its proper position on top of the breastbone (preon), and then you should rectify the fracture and equalize it with those very words.
But if you feel splinters from the collarbone and your hands are sore, then it is necessary that you cut over there and extract those splinters with ease.
And if it is held in the bone, then you should make an incision of it with one of the instruments which you have prepared for this purpose, since you had previously paused behind the collarbone with the instrument that serves the ciphac; and this instrument is a chisel made of wood or iron, whose form is as follows:
And it is similar to a culler whose concavity is as follows: and its latitude should be according to what you have needed of it, according to the size of the bone or the paucity of it.
But the length of it should be according to what is possible at your operation; that there are two extremities thus as times, and one extremity should be broad and the other narrow.
And if the disruption of the wound that you have incised when you have extracted the splinter from the bone is wide, and you are sure that it is a cautious apostema, then you should adjust the two lips of the wound with sutures.
And if the disruption is small or you fear cautious apostema, then you should dress the wound with cloths and powders according to the quantity of the wound's cut.
And if it happens that cautious apostema occurs, then you should dip a cloth in warm vinegar and rose oil and water, and pause over that.
And all, that the plate not be bruised over the broken bone; and for this it is necessary that you see the patient every day, so that when the bond is softened or you see the plate already being remade, then you should correct this and strengthen the binding.
And then, pause the sleep of the patient over the collarbone of it, and pause behind the titillating of it, that is to say, put the sleep of it on the night, a little pillow; so that with this, the assistant of it from the side of that, is elevated, and therefore, the fracture of the collarbone is elevated to elevation of the muscle; or is the arm of it tied to the collarbone.
And do not remove the binding unless it accidentally occurs in the most important or apostemic location within 12 days.
And then, renew the emplastre if you see the face of it to that point, and adjust in the structure and restore it, and leave it until it is restored and the fracture of the collarbone has been coagulated.
And it is strengthened and comforted according to the measure in 28 days, and some times it is done in less time for certain people.
